China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Plans to Improve Business on the Four New Ships 122

The Yuanheng Lizhen Four New Ships of the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, which sail between Hong Kong and Guangdong, are essential to the company's lifeline. Therefore, efforts are constantly made to rectify and improve them. The business and shipbuilding departments often send personnel on board to conduct on-site inspections to improve them. Recently, the general affairs, business, and shipbuilding departments consulted on seventeen reform measures for the Four New Ships, which were issued to each ship yesterday for review and implementation. The original document is as follows: (1) The chief mate, second mate, and purser should supervise the steward to ensure that the food for the passengers is handled properly. (2) Cooks and waiters often sleep soundly and naked on the decks of first-class cabins when it is hot, which is unsightly. The chief mate and second mate should strictly prohibit this. (3) Service staff are often very lazy, and the purser and assistant do not strictly manage them, resulting in messy dishes and even gathering on sofas to chat or nap. The purser should be responsible for strictly prohibiting this. (4) Service staff are not allowed to eat in the main dining room. (5) Entertainment equipment should be placed in the account room and only taken out when guests need entertainment. (6) Haiyuan previously hired an extra hand to wash bowls, which is similar to the "cold water class" system and should be immediately prohibited. (7) After the ship arrives at the port, canvas beds and chairs are placed everywhere, often resulting in loss and damage. The captain, together with the purser, should inspect the ship after it arrives at the port and supervise the service staff to handle them properly. (8) Service staff are not allowed to go ashore after arriving at the port without the purser's permission. If they need to go ashore, they should hand over the keys to the purser and notify the purser of their return time. Those who are late will be considered tardy. The purser should be responsible for supervising all the staff on the ship. (9) Responsible personnel in each department should strictly prohibit the sale of berths. (10) Food should not be placed in the luggage room, and luggage should not be placed in the walkways. (11) The floors of the third-class cabins must be washed clean with water by the service staff after arriving at the port. (12) The first and second-class cabins are not very clean. The purser should effectively lead the service staff to carry out cleaning work. (13) Service staff's wake-up time in the morning is 6 AM in autumn and winter and 5 AM in spring and summer. They are not allowed to sleep late. The purser should inspect to see if anyone is sleeping late at that time. The time for service staff to get up when the ship arrives at the port is determined by the purser. (14) The purser should re-determine the shifts for service staff, with four people per shift. There must also be four people on duty at night, and they should be inspected at any time to prevent them from sleeping. (15) Service staff on the ship should wear uniforms. Those who wear casual clothes will be considered absent from work. (16) The captain, purser, and steward should inspect the passenger areas of the entire ship every day at 11 AM, fill out a report, and send it to the bureau. (17) The captain, purser, and steward should convene service staff and waiters at any time for training, and provide instructions on improving their work.

Tenth Regular Meeting of the Anti-Smoking Association and Visit to the Shanghai North Drug Rehabilitation Hospital 126

The Central News Agency reports that the Shanghai Anti-Smoking Committee's deadline for voluntary registration of smokers in the city will expire at the end of this month. From next month, forced registration will begin. Fearing that smokers do not understand the details and are hesitant, various publicity materials have been drafted, and lecturers have been assigned to form a propaganda team with the Municipal Public Security Bureau to set off in the city and Zhabei 　Dong Gaoqiao area to publicize and lecture, so that smokers can understand the meaning of registration and enthusiastically go to the Public Security Bureau to register. In addition, the committee visited the Shanghai North Drug Rehabilitation Hospital on Tiantong'an Road, Zhabei, at the invitation of Li Qian'an, Director of the Municipal Health Bureau, to inspect the hospital's internal facilities. They also held a meeting in the hospital's conference room. Committee members Shi Xiaolai, Chu Qiaolian, Wang Yiting, Wang Boqi, Du Yuesheng, and the association's secretary Gui Yuhua, Cai Bubai, section chief Lin, and Wang Yu attended. Director Li, Section Chief Shen, and Dean Mei received them and guided them to visit the first, second, and third wards, explaining the methods and procedures of treatment in detail. The wards were well-ventilated, and the food for the smokers was also very sanitary. It is said that smokers who quit and are discharged from the hospital gain an average of five hours in weight. In addition, each room is equipped with a radio to regulate the smokers' minds and bodies so they will not feel lonely. Outside the wards, there are gardens 　 corners for smokers to do light exercise. The committee members praised the hospital's thorough facilities. They then went to the conference room, where they were offered tea and refreshments. Director Li delivered a speech, saying, "I am very honored to have the opportunity to invite everyone here today to visit. Everyone has expertise in the anti-smoking industry, and I hope you will not hesitate to give us your advice. If there is an opportunity in the future, we would like to gather together again to discuss the progress of anti-smoking efforts." Committee member Yan Fuqing then stood up to give a thank-you speech. This was followed by the tenth regular meeting. The attendees were committee members Yan Fuqing, Zai Boqi, Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng (Xiaodai), Chu Qiaoqing, Wang Yiting, and the attendees were Li Tingan, Shen Gao, Mei Zhuosheng, Gui Yuhua, Wang Yu, and Lin Fu. Chairman Yan Fuqing, and recorder Cai Bubai A. Report Items: (1) Reading the resolutions of the previous session, (2) Reporting the work progress. B. Discussion Items: (1) Yan Fuqing proposed that the Municipal Government be requested to transfer the association and the Health Bureau to designate concurrent drug rehabilitation hospitals, so that smokers can voluntarily receive treatment and avoid顾已 cases. The reason attached: This city has allocated funds to establish four free treatment hospitals for drug rehabilitation, which is enough to give smokers a way to reform themselves. However, those who go to receive treatment must first register with the Public Security Bureau, and upon arrival at the hospital, they must have their photos taken and fingerprints taken. To quit addiction, they must also fill out a statement of quitting at the Public Security Bureau. Although the above procedures are for examination and verification, those who have addictions are still hesitant to go forward during the period when forced smoking cessation has not yet been implemented. Those with better financial conditions are even more reluctant to accept future restrictions. At the same time, they are also afraid of seeking medical treatment for smoking cessation, which is too expensive, and the method of smoking cessation is not appropriate. It seems to have an impact on the future of smoking cessation. It is feared that the number of people who voluntarily quit smoking at the moment will decrease because of this. When forced smoking cessation comes, the number of people will be too large. Moreover, the situation in Shanghai is special. Some smokers live in special zones. In order to encourage treatment, it is proposed that this association suggest to the Municipal Government, based on the provisions of Article 4 of the Organizational Regulations, that the Municipal Government consult with the Health Bureau and designate several formal hospitals to concurrently handle smoking cessation, with the government subsidizing a portion of the costs and sending personnel to supervise the hospitals from time to time. The procedures for admission and discharge should generally follow the hospital's regulations, and there is no need to go through the registration, photography, fingerprinting, and signing procedures to avoid hesitation. As for the examination method, the smoking cessation hospital can submit a list of the names, genders, ages, occupations, detailed addresses, admission and discharge dates, and names of doctors who have or have not quit to the Public Security Bureau and this association for compilation and examination on a monthly basis. Whether or not it is appropriate, I hope that a public resolution will be made. (Resolution) Passed. The two municipal governments are requested to check and handle it. Adjourned.

Gu Zhizhong Discusses Impressions of the Newspaper Industry After Returning from Investigating in Europe and America 129

The News Industry in Various Countries is Advancing Rapidly; Our Country Should Strive to Emulate and Improve

The Sheng News Agency reports that Gu Zhizhong, a reporter from the News Newspaper, returned to Shanghai on the afternoon of the day before yesterday after investigating the news industry in Europe and America for about two years, covering about one hundred and ten countries. He was warmly welcomed by colleagues at the North Railway Station and in the local newspaper industry. According to Gu, during his trip abroad to investigate the news industry in various countries, he found that the newspaper industry in all countries is making rapid progress. This is due to the support and assistance of the government and various sectors of society, but also to the hard work and efforts of the staff in the newspaper industry of other countries, which can be emulated by Chinese journalists. When abroad, he had the opportunity to read newspapers from his motherland and felt that the newspaper industry in our country has also made rapid progress in recent years. However, in order to accelerate the advancement of the current stage of the Chinese news industry, our colleagues still need to make continuous efforts. It is reported that Gu will continue to work at the News Newspaper after returning to Shanghai. The reporters of the local newspaper industry have now agreed to have Gu give a second lecture on journalism at the Business School of Shanghai University at 7:00 PM this Saturday (the 19th), focusing on the newspaper industry in Europe and America.

Shanghai Municipal Council Reduces Overseas Travel Expenses for Foreign Staff 130

According to the regulations, foreign employees of the Shanghai Municipal Council are entitled to a long vacation and return to their home country every four to five years, and their travel expenses are paid by the Shanghai Municipal Council. Now, in order to implement austerity measures, the Finance Department has reduced these travel expenses by grade. The heads of all departments and directors of important departments will be given first-class travel expenses, about 172 pounds. Other staff members who previously enjoyed first-class travel expenses will be given 130 pounds. Other staff members who previously enjoyed second-class travel expenses will be given 123 pounds. According to the Finance Department's report, it can save about 65,000 yuan in travel expenses per year. It is reported that this proposal has been approved by the Shanghai Municipal Council's staff remuneration committee and has been approved by the board of directors.

Taxpayers' Association Requests the Municipal Council to Respect Laws and Regulations and Not to Favor Li Quewei 137

Municipal Council Employees Dare to Disobey Regulations, and it is Difficult to Punish Public Buses for Repeated Accidents

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday, stating: "We are writing to inform you that we have received a joint letter from twenty-two citizens, including Zhu Shaohao, Wu Chuncai, and Luo Binqiu, stating that they read in the newspaper that a shocking car accident occurred at the entrance of the Hankou Road Stock Exchange at around 1:00 PM on the 8th of this month. The victim, Mr. Li Chuanbin, was on the sidewalk and was killed by a car driven by Li Quewei, a Westerner from the Municipal Council, who recklessly drove onto the sidewalk. This is a great tragedy. After learning about this, we were all shocked and extremely disturbed. Therefore, we are writing to you to request that the Municipal Council negotiate with reason and severely punish the Western employee who caused the accident, so as to ensure that other Western drivers will not dare to commit similar tragedies in the future, to appease public anger and protect the safety of pedestrians. We were processing this matter when we received a letter from Mr. Li Chuansi, the brother of the deceased, stating, "My younger brother, Chuanbin, a native of Wuxian, was 23 years old and worked as a wireless telegraph operator for the Shanghai branch of the Central News Agency. At 1:55 PM on the 8th of this month, he was walking east on the south sidewalk of Hankou Road from his dormitory at Tongan Lane to the news agency office in the Continental Mansion. Unexpectedly, when he reached the door of 421 Fuyong Silk Store (next to the Shanghai Hotel) on that road, Li Quewei C.H. Ridgway, an inspector from the Municipal Council's Revenue Office, drove a concession-plated car No. 8497 eastward without following traffic regulations, driving onto the south sidewalk and knocking my brother down from behind, breaking his leg bones, injuring his internal organs, and destroying the window sill of Fuyong Store. My brother only cried out for help once before losing consciousness. The Fuyong Store called the police and the Red Cross Society sent an ambulance to the scene for emergency treatment. He was taken to Renji Hospital, but died of his injuries. I received the news and rushed to Shanghai overnight, but my brother's body was already at the Forensic Examination Office on Helun Road. At 10:00 AM on the 9th, Judge Pei from the Shanghai First Special District Court questioned the Westerner Li Quewei, who admitted the circumstances of the accident, but falsely claimed that the accident was caused by the slippery road due to rain. The police and vehicle officials, who are also British, said that my brother was walking on the sidewalk and was not at fault, but the accident was unavoidable due to the slippery road. Their statement is absurd and hateful. According to regulations, Hankou Road is a one-way street from west to east, and cars should drive in the middle. However, the Westerner, relying on being an employee of the Municipal Council, did not follow the regulations and drove recklessly, causing this disaster. I immediately requested the court to detain the Westerner, but because the defendant is British, it could not be done according to the law. I think that if cars can recklessly drive onto the sidewalk and injure pedestrians without responsibility due to slippery roads, then no country would have such a law. Otherwise, the sidewalk can be renamed the car lane. How can the lives of pedestrians be protected? My brother's sacrifice is a small matter, but the safety of all citizens is a major concern. I am reporting the incident with tears and begging for justice and fairness. Moreover, Hankou Road is a one-way street, and the speed of cars is regulated. Cars should proceed in an orderly manner. Even if the road was slippery, no other roads with heavier traffic than Hankou Road that day, or cars driving on Hankou Road, had similar accidents. The fact that Inspector Li Quewei caused the accident proves that he did not follow traffic regulations and recklessly disregarded human life, causing this disaster. Furthermore, Li Quewei is an employee of your Bureau, and he dares to disobey the traffic regulations set by your Bureau. Your Bureau should find it difficult to excuse him for the accident in the same way that you punish Chinese public buses for repeated accidents. Based on the above, we hereby request that your Bureau respect the traffic regulations it has set and not abandon them. The employee Li Quewei should be immediately reported and suspended from duty, and the matter should be judged fairly according to the law to appease the people and uphold justice, so that humanity and the law can be maintained to satisfy the public."

Male Robbers Arrested Upstairs in a Pancake Shop 138

One Thief Pulled Out a Gun and Tried to Resist Arrest; All Criminals Admitted to Planning a Robbery

Detective Shang Wu of the Huizhi Police Station received a tip-off the other day that a gang of thieves was gathering upstairs at a pancake shop at 125 Baker Road, plotting illegal activities. He and Western Detective Yang went to the address at 6:30 PM the day before yesterday and arrested seven thieves: Li Yueqing, Hu Xueming, Gu Qingyu, Wang A'er, Xu Zhande, Zhang Wenqi, and a woman, Xu Wangshi. They were all taken to the police station, detained separately, and escorted to the Criminal Court of the First Special Court yesterday morning. Zhang Tianyin, the police lawyer, requested that all the arrested criminals be detained. The defendants, after being arrested, admitted that they intended to rob the city that night and gathered there beforehand. Li Yueqing, Hu Xueming, and Xu Zhande confessed to robbing two households at 49 Lane 4 and Lane 336 on Tongfu Road in June and July of this year. Chen Lan, Who Once Escaped, Was Arrested Again, and Plotted a Second Jailbreak 139

He Sawed Through His Shackles and Two Iron Bars of His Cell; Three Bed Sheets Were Torn and Twisted into a Rope More Than Ten Feet Long

—His Actions Were Discovered by the Guard Before He Could Make a Move—

Murderer Chen Jinlan, nicknamed Snake Skin Jinlan, 32 years old, was involved in the murder of Chen Zhikui, the owner of the Qianfeng Feng Candle Shop on Xinqiao Street on the evening of April 14, 22nd year of the Republic of China, along with Zhu Quanxing from Wuxi. Zhu was arrested first, and Chen fled back to his hometown. In January of the following year, the French police sent officers to Ningbo to arrest Chen and bring him to Shanghai, where he was sentenced to 14 years in prison by the Second Special Court. After appeals to the High Third Branch Court and the Supreme Court, the sentence was reduced to 12 years. Chen was detained in the detention center of the Second Special Court and was about to be executed when he suddenly escaped from prison on December 27th of the previous year, resulting in the dismissal of the warden and the prosecution of guards Fang Yuqi and Zhou Wenjin. Fang was sentenced to two years and six months in prison, and Zhou was sentenced to two years. They appealed, but

Chen Escaped

and went to Hankou. Unable to make a living, he sneaked back to Shanghai and hid in the home of his fellow villager Bian Wuchang at 32 Lao Yong'an Street. On April 15th of this year, Detective Yang Zhongfang and Lu Dongliang of the Baofang detected and arrested Chen, and brought him to the Second Special Court, where he was sentenced to four years in prison. Chen appealed to the High Third Branch Court, which reduced the sentence to one year and six months. On August 16th, the High Third Branch Court sent Chen to the Second Special Prison to serve a sentence of 13 years and six months, stipulating that the time he had previously spent in the detention center would be deducted, and the sentence would expire in the year

37th of the Republic of China

on January 28th. After Chen was arrested, Warden Gao Xiaopian was reinstated by order of the ministry, as Chen's escape did not occur during Fang and Zhou's shift. Therefore, the High Third Branch Court declared them not guilty. After Chen was arrested, it was learned that he escaped at around 1:00 AM, during the shift of internal and external guards Yang Xingcun and Yan Ling. Yang and Yan were detained and transferred to the Second Special Court, where the prosecutor's office brought charges. After a trial by the Criminal Court, they were fined and dismissed. This is a historical dispute regarding Chen's escape. After Chen entered prison, he was assigned number 447 and detained in cell number 1 on the fourth floor of Block A. It was unexpected that the criminal in prison, regarding his

Undying Ambition

to escape, recently planned another jailbreak and acquired a steel saw about five inches long. After preparing everything, at 9:15 PM on the evening of the thirteenth (August), when all the prisoners were asleep, he crouched on the ground and peeked out of the iron door, and was discovered by guard Gong Keyuan (29 years old, from Anhui) on patrol, who secretly ordered another guard, Jin Zhenduo (37 years old, from Anhui), to report to Warden Mao Shun. According to Datong News Agency, the Municipal Private Wireless Broadcasting Industry Association, in view of the severe flooding in various provinces and the recent cold weather, urgently needing rescue, has specially united with the variety arts community to hold a three-day variety show. Variety Show Grand Event

The association previously collected disaster relief funds for flood victims from wireless listeners and frequently promoted fundraising through the airwaves, achieving considerable success. Recently, due to the increasingly cold weather, it has specially joined forces with Guangyu Society, Sutan Research Association, Shanghai Opera Research Association, Drama Research Association, famous Shanghai Opera performers, Cantonese opera masters, singers, and movie stars to launch a variety show to raise funds, officially named "Fundraising Variety Show for Flood Relief in Various Provinces." All members of the conference, report speakers, staff, etc., have been hired on a rotational basis. During the conference period, all broadcasting stations in the city will suspend broadcasting. All advertisements will also cease, as this event is purely for charitable purposes. Special agreement has already been subtly obtained from various contracted stores, with no make-up compensation.

Grand Opening Tomorrow

The conference is scheduled to open tomorrow afternoon at [time]. There will be no opening ceremony. The conference period will run from the 18th to the 20th, a total of three days. Each day will be divided into daytime (starting at 1:00 PM) and evening (starting at 7:00 PM) sessions. Sales have already begun at Yamei Company, Zhongxi Pharmacy, Lili Native Products Company, Bund Hotel, and various radio stations. During the conference period, a ticket sales booth will also be set up at the entrance of the Lake Society. Lei Wen Petitions for Bankruptcy, Willing to Abide by the Court's Judgment 142

According to the Da Mei Evening News, Mr. He Fu, the liquidator of three companies, including American Feng Bank, previously sued Lei Wen in the U.S. Court for China for illegally receiving remunerations of 135,000 taels each from American Sheng Bank, American Dong Bank, and Puyi Real Estate Company, requesting the court to order the payment of interest. The case was heard this morning (16th) by Chief Justice Hillermeck. First, Dr. Xue Laite, the lawyer for Mr. He Fu, stated that an agreement had been reached to merge the three cases. The original plaintiff requested the repayment of the remuneration received from the three companies with interest. However, since the funds from American Dong Bank had been repaid by Lei Wen, only the interest from January 1932 to February 23, 1933, at an annual rate of 6%, was requested. Subsequently, Mr. Lei Wen's lawyer, Mr. Evans, announced that Mr. Lei Wen was willing to abide by the court's judgment and would soon file for bankruptcy voluntarily. Therefore, Mr. Hillermeck stated that since the defendant had this intention, there was nothing to be done in court and ordered Mr. Xue Laite to draft the judgment and send it to Mr. Evans before adjourning the court. Although Mr. Lei Wen was present in court today, he did not say a word. Due to today's developments, the court will issue an order for Mr. Lei Wen to pay the funds requested by Mr. He Fu and will appoint a custodian to manage Mr. Lei Wen's assets to liquidate them for repayment. After the adjournment, Mr. Evans stated that Mr. Lei Wen's bankruptcy petition would likely be filed within this week and that he would invite his creditors, including representatives of the three closed companies and the custodian of Puyi Real Estate Company, to participate in a meeting to elect a custodian of Mr. Lei Wen's assets. It is reported that Mr. Lei Wen's residence on Hongqiao Road will also be included in his assets. Mr. Evans' statement in court today was lengthy. After he finished, Mr. Xue Laite stated that Mr. Evans' statement did not mention Mr. Lei Wen's embezzlement and receipt of funds from Puyi Bank. Mr. Evans replied that Mr. Lei Wen denied ever receiving funds from the company and had never engaged in any fraudulent activities. The courtroom was extremely crowded today, and additional seating was added on both sides to accommodate the audience.

Strange Incident with Lili Automobile: Circular Hole in the Glass 143

A Loud Bang, Smaller on the Outside, Larger on the Inside. Passengers in the Car Showed No Unusual Behavior.

At 10:30 AM yesterday, the Third Branch of Lili Automobile Company on Avenue de Sapey in the French Concession received a phone call from Qingxin Middle School on Lujiabang Road in the Nanshi area, requesting to hire a car to be sent to Zhengyi Middle School in Fahuazhen. Upon delivering the customer to Fahua and returning to the branch, he immediately reported the incident to the accountant. However, after inquiring with nearby shops and residents, all stated that they had not heard any gunshots at the time. The most peculiar thing was that the hole on the window was smaller on the outside and larger on the inside, the outer hole as small as a grain of rice, and the inner hole as large as a longan, resembling a shot from inside the car to the outside. However, at the time, there was only one customer inside the car, and the customer showed no unusual behavior. The police are currently investigating.

Key Suspect Luo Yusheng Demonstrates the Two Murders 147

Judges and Clerks Listen Quietly in the Next Room; Luo Admits His Guilt Only After Seeing the Judge

The wife of the late former Ningbo District Court Prosecutor Jin Zhaojin, Jin Dai Shi, also known as Baozhen, and her children lived on the third floor of 459 North Henan Road, near the intersection of Elgin Road. On the morning of the 23rd of last month, she was found murdered in her bedroom. The hired maid, Ms. Luo, was also murdered. Afterwards, detective Shang Wu from the relevant Huishi Police Station arrested the key suspect, Luo Yusheng, a native of Yiwu, Zhejiang, and the current director of academic affairs at Mingchen Elementary School on Xinqiao Road in Nanshi. The victims' property and an axe were recovered. The case was transferred to the First Special District Local Court for repeated interrogations. As reported previously, Judge Liu Yugui, in charge of the case, found that Luo always denied the murders during the trials. However, according to Detective Shang's report, Luo confessed in the police station that he colluded with a man surnamed Xu and a man surnamed Ma, meeting at the intersection of North Henan Road and Laobazi Road, and then going to Jin Dai Shi's residence. Taking advantage of the absence of her children, who had gone to school, he kept watch downstairs while Xu and Ma went upstairs and murdered Jin Dai Shi and the maid. Then he entered the room to steal property. When Luo was confronted with this information, he claimed that the confession was coerced by the police, making it difficult to determine the truth. To clarify the truth and avoid wrongly accusing anyone, Judge Liu, accompanied by the clerk and trial lawyer Zhang Tianyin from the police station, went to the scene of the crime at 459 North Henan Road, near the intersection of Elgin Road, on the afternoon of the previous day. After inspecting the scene, they went to rest in a small room next to the victim's bedroom. After a while, Detective Shang and others brought Luo Yusheng upstairs to the victim's bedroom and asked him about the murders. Luo, initially unaware that the judge, clerk, police station, and lawyer were in the adjacent room, and unguarded, spoke freely as he had in the police station. He recounted how he had kept watch downstairs while Xu and Ma murdered Jin Dai Shi and the maid, and then how he went upstairs to steal property. Detective Shang and others waited until he had finished speaking before taking him to the adjacent room. Luo, upon seeing the judge sitting there, the clerk recording his previous statements, was shocked and lost color. Judge Liu then asked, "You have repeatedly claimed in court that your confession in the police station was coerced. Now, there is no coercion of any kind, and you have confessed so much yourself. Your confession must be sincere." The clerk then read the transcript aloud. Luo bowed his head and confessed his guilt. Judge Liu, knowing that before the crime, the perpetrators had met at the intersection of North Henan Road and Laobazi Road, wanted to clarify the facts. He ordered a car to be driven to that location, with Luo being escorted by Detective Shang. A patrolman was stationed there. Judge Liu ordered Luo to demonstrate where he had gotten out of the car, where Xu and Ma were waiting, how he held the axe, who was in front and who was behind when they left. Luo's demonstration was vivid. The patrolman drove away bystanders to maintain order while observing the demonstration, so he could testify in court today. Luo, though cunning, would find it difficult to deny the facts. Judge Liu's handling of this case was particularly painstaking.

It is now decided to announce and implement them from the 16th of this month. In addition to reporting to the superiors and notifying the relevant departments, the above regulations are hereby copied, published in the newspaper, and announced to all Chinese and foreign residents of the city. The copied Shanghai Provisional Hunting Regulations are as follows: Article 1. Hunting, as referred to in these regulations, means capturing birds and animals with shotguns, nets, or other mechanical devices. Article 2. No person may hunt without being approved by the Public Security Bureau and obtaining a permit, except when not using mechanical devices within their own property. Article 3. Hunters may not use the following methods to capture birds and animals: 1. Explosives. 2. Poisons. 3. Potent drugs. 4. Traps. Article 4. Hunters may not engage in hunting in the following places: 1. Historical sites. 2. Parks. 3. Public roads. 4. Temples and monasteries. 5. Places where crowds gather. 6. Military areas. 7. Other places designated by the Public Security Bureau or approved by the people as prohibited hunting areas. Article 5. The following categories of people may not hunt: 1. Minors. 2. People with mental disorders. 3. Soldiers or police officers. 4. Those who have been punished under these regulations within the past year. Article 6. Hunters may not hunt at night without special permission. Article 7. The Municipal Government and the Public Security Bureau may suspend hunting in any of the following circumstances: 1. When martial law is declared. 2. When bandits are discovered. 3. When the birds and animals permitted to be hunted need protection. 4. When the hunting grounds permitted to be hunted need to be closed. Article 8. Hunters may not enter other people's gardens, cultivated land, or fenced land to hunt without the consent of the owner. Article 9. Birds and animals prohibited from being hunted by laws and regulations may not be hunted, except for research purposes with the approval of the government. Article 10. Hunters must carry their shotgun license and hunting permit when hunting for inspection by the police, and must not impersonate others or use expired permits. Article 11. The hunting season is from October 1st each year to the end of March of the following year. If there are special circumstances, the Public Security Bureau may extend the period, but the extension may not exceed the end of April of the following year. Article 12. Hunters must first fill out an application form, detailing their name, age, address, type of hunting equipment, hunting location, etc., and attach a recent photograph. After being reviewed by the Public Security Bureau, a hunting permit will be issued. Hunters may only hunt in the locations specified on the permit. Article 13. Hunting permits are divided into two types: Type A costs one yuan in national currency, and Type B costs two yuan in national currency. However, those using foreign shotguns and other hunting equipment may not apply for a Type A permit. Article 14. Violations of Articles 2 to 13 of these regulations will be punished in accordance with Article 5 of the Administrative Execution Law, and their hunting permits may be revoked. Article 15. These regulations are applicable before the implementation of the new hunting law and will be repealed on the date of the implementation of the new hunting law. Article 16. These regulations shall be approved and promulgated by the Municipal Government for implementation.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 161

— (Huanglian)

"People should be independent and also cooperative." Everyone knows these two sentences.

However, "independence" and "cooperation" are interconnected: neither is dispensable!

If there is only "independence" but no "cooperation"! Then it is like "a heap of loose sand!"

Conversely, if there is only "cooperation"! But no "independence!" Then it becomes a bustling "mass of parasites!"

Because it is necessary for everyone to be "independent"! To increase the strength of "cooperation!"

It is like ten arrows, each broken, then putting them together is useless. Ten arrows, none broken. Putting them together, then it is not easy to break!

Everyone "cooperates!" to consolidate the bulwark of "independence!" For example, a piece of iron, a furnace of fire, will naturally melt it. Gather hundreds of pieces of iron together, and a furnace of fire will have no way to melt it.

Therefore, I hope that the four hundred and fifty million compatriots! Everyone must have the spirit of "independence"! At the same time, there must also be the organization of "cooperation!" This is a new line of hope for the future of the country!

Proof of Crystallization 162

— Fieldsman

My neighbor, Mr. Fang, is already sixty years old, and is a Confucian gentleman who does not look at or speak of anything improper. Because he only has two beloved daughters who are both married, and has no son to inherit his legacy, not only is Mr. Fang himself often worried, but he also often suffers the ridicule of his sister-in-law, making him even more unhappy. This is what led Mr. Fang to "rent a wife."

One evening, I remember Mr. Fang, holding a dry tobacco pipe in his left hand and an almanac in his right, walking slowly to chat with my grandmother. My grandmother, wrinkling her forehead and pursing her lips, smiled with her old eyes at Mr. Fang and said, "I heard that the country wife—that is, Mr. Fang's newly rented wife—is eating red eggs. Congratulations! Congratulations! In the future, when you have a little Binnsay, we will all have to drink a few more cups of wine." Mr. Fang replied with a chuckle, "The red eggs are being eaten, but I can't guarantee whether it will be a boy or a girl. Amitabha, it all depends on the help of the Bodhisattva!" As he spoke, he puffed out smoke from his mouth like clouds. Standing in front of my grandmother's knee, I thought: Maybe Mr. Fang was just "chanting."

Mr. Fang knocked the tobacco ash off the ground with his pipe, then flipped through a few pages of the almanac and handed it to my grandmother. I peeked at it, and saw a small red circle marked on × month ×× day. I was very surprised. I saw Mr. Fang extend his thin, long finger and point to the red circle, saying: On this day, I went to the country to spend the night with my wife. Now I have this small red circle as proof. Counting it, she is already three months pregnant. My grandmother said: Hmm! I see.

Now, young Mr. Fang is already twenty-one years old, although his appearance and demeanor are not very similar to Mr. Fang. When I recall this interesting story, if anyone doubts it, I am willing to be a witness. I wonder if this "proof of crystallization" almanac still exists today?

Recent Salt Crisis 163

— Yiqiu

In the area of the two seacoasts of Yuyao, hundreds of miles, live ten thousand salt farmers, relying on their blood and sweat, strength, in the scorching sun and salt water, to earn a family's food and clothing. Each pound of salt can only sell for two or three copper coins, and their lives are very miserable and pitiful. Recently, salt barns have stopped collecting extra salt due to accumulated inventory, further plunging them into despair.

Due to the above reasons, a great crisis has arisen among the salt farmers in the Xiangongdian area in the past two days. Many salt farmers surrounded the salt barns, forcing them to open the scales, but the barns, due to years of losses and accumulated inventory, insisted on not allowing it. The two sides clashed many times, almost causing a riot. Later, after persuasion, the salt farmers elected representatives to go to the Salt Commissioner's Office in Hangzhou to petition. Most of the responsible managers of the barns did not dare to live in the barns and fled to other places.

As for the reason for the accumulated inventory in the salt barns, it is due to the impact of refined salt dumping. According to people in the salt barns: "The salt transport in Jiangsu and Zhejiang is a tax-inclusive monopoly system. For example, a certain salt merchant pays a certain amount of tax every year and has the exclusive right to transport salt in a certain area. In the past, the salt barns always had a surplus every year, the taxes could be paid, and the salt farmers had food to eat. But in recent years, the government has also allowed the transportation and sale of refined salt. Refined salt is produced in the north, and because the purchase price is low, the price is not higher than that of coarse salt from Yuyao. More and more people in the folk are changing to eat refined salt, and the power of refined salt is growing day by day, filling various places and encroaching on the market of coarse salt, so the salt barns are losing money every year, and the salt farmers in Yuyao are in danger."

Although, recently, it is said that the Zhejiang Salt Transport Commissioner has drafted a compromise solution, allowing the salt barns to collect salt at 60% of the quota, it is still a question whether the salt farmers will agree and whether the barns can sell the new salt collected at this 60% rate. Even if the salt farmers agree, but the barns already have accumulated inventory, and if they collect new goods and they remain unsold, it is difficult to guarantee that the old tune will not be repeated next year—stopping the collection of extra salt—I think this is not a fundamental solution. The rice for two people can never be combined to feed one person! I hope that the wise authorities will understand this point and make a thorough reform. I, as a small person, dare not defend the salt merchants, but I really cannot bear to see the hundreds of thousands of salt farmers who are already in despair, and I know the key problem but dare not remain silent.

Little Western Paradise 165

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 20: Struggling for Life to See Beloved Grandson, Embracing Each Other and Shedding Tears, Remembering the Past in a Famine Year, Sowing Wheat and Bringing Disaster

The old lady didn't say anything, put her withered, waxy left hand around him, and tears fell like thrown sand. Yueying sobbed, Zhu Hu's held his sleeves and sobbed too. Sister-in-law Hu stood on the side, looking at these three generations, at their miserable situation, and couldn't help but feel pain in her heart, and started crying with the three of them. This immediately alarmed all the travelers in the inn, who gathered around to watch. When they asked what happened, although they couldn't openly criticize Jia Duocai for being wrong, they all nodded and sighed at the silent frustration. As everyone watched, the tea room saw that the situation was getting out of hand, so he found Sister-in-law Hu and said: Hey! You know the situation here, you brought these people here to cry for no reason, what kind of look is that? If Mr. Jia comes back, I can't afford it. You guys go away! Old lady Zhu wiped away her tears and said: I can't leave, I will die if I leave. I finally got to see my child, how can I leave? The tea room said: If you don't leave, are you planning to stay in our lobby forever? This is a thoroughfare. Sister-in-law Hu saw that these three generations were clinging to each other, and it was not easy to tear them apart suddenly, so she frowned and said: I don't have the strength to make them leave immediately. We don't dare to enter Mr. Jia's room randomly, I think we should find a small room here and let them sit down and talk for a while, and when they finish saying what they want to say, they will naturally disperse. The tea room smiled indifferently: You said it so easily, we opened a room and let them go in to talk, who will pay for the room? The smallest room costs eighty cents a day. (341)

Imperial Fragrance Ephemeral Record 166

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Although the appearance of these bathtubs is the same, they all have secret signs underneath to distinguish their uses, and they must not be confused. (If they are accidentally confused, the Empress Dowager will definitely not let it go.)—Filled with warm water, it was lifted all the way to the Empress Dowager's feet before being placed down. The Empress Dowager then immersed both feet in the basin, and the four palace maids, following the previous method, soaped her, changed towels, and continued to apply the Camellia Oil. I watched coldly from the side, and soon discovered that the skills of the four palace maids were indeed exceptionally skilled and agile. They knew how much force to use to wring the soaked towels almost dry, how much soap to apply to the towels, and how gently to rub off the dirt without causing the Empress Dowager pain, and how to pat the oil dry; obviously, these skills could not be mastered overnight. Then the effort they spent learning in the beginning must have been very long! I think it would not be an exaggeration to treat them as specialized artisans.

After washing the lower body, the Empress Dowager immediately put on her trousers, and the bathing process was declared complete. But wait, there is still a final procedure! The four palace maids had to take another set (four) of new towels to wipe the Empress Dowager's fingers and face. After all, I don't quite remember how many times new towels were changed, but let me tell you, there are ten palace maids in the palace who do nothing all day except wash the Empress Dowager's clothes, etc. You can know that even if the old lady uses forty towels every time she washes, it is not impossible! (437)

Sweet Osmanthus and Chestnuts 167

— (Zhang Mengzhao)

The fragrance of sweet osmanthus and the opening of golden chestnut barrels indicate that it is already the mid-autumn season! White clouds caress my house, and I often dream of my lovely hometown, Wuxi. I remember in the autumn of a certain year, the farmers who rented the graveyard offered Du chestnuts for sale, their fragrance was refreshing and their golden color was lovely. They were indeed the genuine goods from Niangniangtang in Huishan, and one yuan could buy half a kilogram. After removing the skin, mix them with Hunan lotus seeds and cook them for breakfast. You don't need to add much sugar to feel that they are fragrant and sweet. Sweet osmanthus and chestnuts are not easy to cultivate, and the yield is very small. In the past, there were many customer chestnuts that were used as fake, and the villagers were very angry. They asked my friend Lawyer Jiang Gongjian to warn and protect them, and they gradually disappeared. This year, because someone bought the whole batch with a hundred taels of gold, the market price is extremely high, and one tael of gold can only buy fourteen taels.

General Knowledge

Sweat 168

— Chuyu

When we arrive in summer, we often develop a strong body odor, which varies depending on race (white or yellow) and gender (male or female). However, the body odor that each person emits is mainly sweat, so it can also be called sweat odor. A person's sweat odor varies depending on their diet. That is, the sweat glands that secrete on the surface of each person's skin play an excretory role in the body's functions through the lungs, kidneys, stomach, and other organs. When the weather is hot, the blood vessels in the skin expand, and the secretion of sweat glands is particularly strong. That is, the secretion of sweat glands releases the excess body temperature to the outside, so after we sweat, we can regulate body temperature. Just like when the body is sick, with chills and fever, if you take antipyretic medicine, the sweat glands will secrete, and then you will break into a sweat, and the heat can be relieved immediately. As such, sweat and hygiene are really closely related. Now we need to pay attention to the following points: (1) Decayed sweat will stimulate the skin. Sweat is secreted and quickly decays, so it produces a strange odor. Sweat odor stimulates the skin very severely. Children are often stimulated by sweat odor, which reduces the skin's resistance, and they are prone to eczema and sores. Therefore, after sweating, it should be washed immediately to prevent accumulation. Women with very long hair accumulate a lot of sweat, which can easily cause hair loss. (2) Sweating while sleeping is very dangerous, because people who are sound asleep experience a decrease in body temperature after sweating, which can easily cause colds. In severe cases, it can cause pleurisy and pulmonary catarrh. If a person is mentally tired and has a weak chest, sweating while sleeping is a type of fatigue toxin and is extremely unsuitable. Therefore, to prevent sweating while sleeping, you can drink a cup of warm milk before going to bed. (3) There is also a type of armpit odor, which is even more uncomfortable. Armpit odor is mostly caused by the development of sexual desire. There is no armpit odor in childhood, and the armpit odor of men and women is different, which is related to sexual dimorphism. As for the most intense body odor in the body, the part where the sweat glands are densely packed is the greatest, that is, the armpits, palms, soles, groins, etc. (4) In general, diet has a great influence on sweat. For example, after eating breakfast, the ingredients of the food are mixed into the sweat and excreted outside the skin. Northerners like to eat green onions and garlic, so they have the smell of green onions and garlic. When musk deer reach puberty, they secrete aromatic substances in their reproductive glands. (5) Among all the races in the world, the body odor is the greatest in black people, followed by white people. However, body odor will also decrease with age, because the functions of the elderly have been closed off. It is said that Concubine Yang was very beautiful, but she had two major problems, namely bad breath and armpit odor. Emperor Tang Ming asked the imperial physician to give her lychees, which gradually eliminated the bad breath, and used perfume to bathe to relieve the armpit odor. The King of Peru liked body odor the most. When he chose a queen, he ordered the noble women to gather in a dark dance floor. After the women danced for half an hour, when their bodies sweated, the king would burrow into the women, and the one with the strongest body odor would be chosen as the queen. This peculiar habit is truly unique, similar to the habit of eating scabs.

Literary News - There were the most essays in the Ming Dynasty. Famous writers were praised by contemporaries. Yuan Zongdao, Yuan Hongdao, and Yuan Zhongdao of the Gong'an School and Zhong Xing and Tan Yuanchun of the Jingling School were considered outstanding essayists of the Ming Dynasty. In fact, writers such as Xu Wenchang and Tang Bohu in the flourishing period of the Ming Dynasty and Chen Jiru and Tang Xianzu in the late Ming Dynasty were not necessarily above the Yuan and Zhong School. Now the owner of Dadao Bookstore has specially released his family's collection of Xu Wenchang, Chen Jiru, Tang Xianzu, Tang Bohu, Zhu Yunming, and Wen Zhengming's complete works, compiled into the Complete Works of Six Famous Essayists of the Ming Dynasty, and handed it over to Jiuzhou Bookstore on Fourth ____ Road for pre-sale. The entire set of eleven thick volumes is priced at 26 yuan. A 15% discount pre-sale only costs 3 yuan and 6 jiao, and single varieties can also be ordered separately. There is also a hardcover version available for scholars to collect. Pre-sales are scheduled to end at the end of this month. It is scheduled that the complete works of Xu Wenchang and Chen Jiru will be published first on November 10.

Long-Term Loans Still Tight 172

The current (i.e. the end of October) long-term funding, for various expiring long-term settlements, and the situation of new transactions, feels quite deserted. At this time when long-term loans are most needed, in previous years there would be at least three or four points of achievement that could be announced. Now, because banks and money shops are seeking to secure their own foundations, most are unwilling to indulge in indiscriminate lending, even a small transaction of one or two thousand must go through a serious investigation and require a reliable shop guarantee before it can be done. Otherwise, simply transferring the old loans that cannot be recovered is already a favor. It is naturally impossible to ask for new loans. Therefore, at present, ordinary shops, because their own economies are insufficient, have always relied on the financial community for long-term loans to help with turnover, but now they have nowhere to turn. According to yesterday's market situation, money shops did slightly open up a small number of long-term loans, but they were only small transactions of two or three thousand and five or six thousand, and there were no reports of transactions over 10,000. These small transactions all have considerable guarantees, and the interest rates are all above 9 yuan, with terms of six months and five months. The total amount is less than 100,000. As for long-term deposits that have expired, since the previous day (the 15th) has passed, those expiring on the 20th of this time are about 1 million. Although half of them have been transferred, the money shops feel it is difficult to return half of them and must wait until the due date to determine. This year's mainland gangs, such as Su, Xi, Chang, Song, Jia, He, Hang, and Hu, both deposits and loans have a long-term term. Yesterday, it was reported that most of the long-term deposits must be repaid, and most of the long-term loans owed may not be able to be repaid as desired. According to reliable news from the financial community, money shop peers are now privately setting long-term repayment methods. Those who truly cannot repay their debts should not be forced to do the impossible and should be allowed to transfer the debts, but the term cannot follow the old precedent (six months) and must be determined according to the situation, either three months or four months, so as not to harm the harmony of the business.

Yarn and Cotton Prices: Spot Gold Closes at a Peak; Surge in Yarn Prices Resumes

Speculators are scrambling to cover their positions, and sentiment is high. The previously sluggish yarn market has suddenly become extremely active. In reality, cotton yarn sales have been quite brisk recently, and factory inventories have decreased significantly. Given favorable news, the upward pressure is even stronger.

Grain: Instability Remains in Flour and Wheat Markets 177

The flour market opened in the morning with a sharp rise, followed by a return to flat. Foreign quotations showed Chicago up by 3 to 5 cents, and Canada up by 2 to 3. Market sentiment was initially buoyant due to rising foreign wheat prices and persistent inflation rumors, leading to strong buying interest. Prices rose by 1 to 2 cents across all months. Subsequently, buying interest waned, and inflation rumors subsided, causing the market to return to flat. In the afternoon, trading was lighter, and the market saw a lack of development in buying and selling due to the international situation remaining serious and rumors circulating about domestic political issues.

Silk and Tea: Shanghai Silk Dealers Also Suffer from Shortages 179

Market Sentiment is Unusually Bullish

Since silk prices in New York and Yokohama have been rising frequently, Lyon has also been purchasing goods at new high prices. Recently, overseas orders have been quite active. Due to insufficient supply in the ports, silk prices are also trending towards peaks. Amidst the sluggishness of various industries, the silk market appears to have further upside potential. Yesterday, Ren Ji and Mitsui competed for over 300 bales of white factory silk, with unusually high prices reported.

Oil Market: Sharp Drop in New White Tung Oil 180

Selling at Half the Price is Inappropriate

Since the closure of foreign firms in Hankou, the market for white tung oil has become precarious. New oil has arrived in Shanghai, with prices opening at $45 per load, a drop of around $40 compared to old oil, selling at half the price. This is an unprecedented situation. Futures opened at $40, but foreign firms are not eager to take spot oil, so there is no distinction between futures and spot prices. Foreign firms have sent telegrams to Europe and America for inquiries, but there have been no replies. The overseas market has experienced a slight pause, and the market's decline is within expectations. The peak season for new oil is approaching, and a price of $40 may not be sustainable.

Free Talk

Impressions of the National Woodcut Exhibition 183

— Tang Tao

By now, probably no one would doubt the artistic status of woodcuts. But just two or three years ago, they were being scorned by great painters or great talkers, just like the current essays, as unworthy of entering the art world. But what is the situation now? Thanks to the efforts of several young artists, woodcut painting has regained its head, not only progressing but also becoming widespread and powerful, becoming the vanguard of popular art, enough to tear down the sacred banner of art-for-art's-sakeists and add a bit of life to the silent art scene.

For this reason, I was very happy to visit this National Woodcut Exhibition.

This joint exhibition was first held in Beiping, then Tianjin, Jinan, Hankou, and Taiyuan. This is the sixth time, in Shanghai. As an amateur and a casual browser, I still found it interesting, which shows how deeply touching the woodcuts are.

In addition to modern woodcuts, the exhibition also includes displays of ancient prints, folk New Year pictures, woodcut tools, etc., totaling over 700 pieces. The ancient prints are mostly Ming editions, but there are also Song, Yuan, and Jin works, mostly illustrations from Buddhist scriptures and folk novels. The New Year pictures are mostly from Wang Mazi of Beiping, which are also the best.

But the main thing, of course, is the modern woodcuts. Although the works in this section are immature, they are relatively clear, energetic, and closely related to real life. Ancient prints are neither as profound, nor are folk New Year pictures as lively. This is truly a valuable harvest for the Chinese art world in the past two or three years.

These works include originals and imitations of world masterpieces. For example, Li Hua's "Angry Horse" and Lai Shaoqi's "Youth" are two very successful imitations. In terms of original works, the most noteworthy are many works by Yefu. This writer's achievements are very consistent, and the selection of subjects seems to have been carefully considered, such as "The First Sound of Construction," "The Road is Like a Tiger's Mouth," and "Funeral Procession." As for "Flood," "Big Belly Salt" (see this publication), and "Sadness," although they are drawn from serial comics, the exquisite carving, the powerful imagery, and the skilled technique all indicate that he is a very promising woodcut artist.

Luo Qingzhen's early works are quite capable of combining the strengths of Yefu, but he seems to be changing his style now. He has changed from using large knives and axes to fine needles and dense threads, which seems to be a bit weaker in terms of strength. However, his "Cow" and "Returning from Pasture" are still rare.

In addition, Zhang Wang's "Beggar," XXX's "Same Face," Chen Baozhen's "Strength," Duan Ganqing's "Two Hands," Dai Yinlang's "Staring Eyes," Yu Tao's "Debt Collection," Wo XXX's "Meal in the Field," Wang Xingshuan's "Begging," and Zhang Hui's "Busy Farming" and "The Future is Bright" are all very vigorous and interesting, and are undoubtedly excellent works.

Looking at this woodcut exhibition, I think the most successful thing is the facial expressions of the characters. Almost every artist pays attention to this. Not to mention "Staring Eyes," "Same Face," etc., even several portraits, such as Duan Ganqing's portrait of Gandhi, Yang Tian's portrait of Barbusse, and Deng Qing's portrait, etc., are probably taken from photographs, but they are all very realistic and vivid.

What is even more rare are Yefu's two brick books, which is a new attempt. Brick carvings are more economical than woodcuts. Judging from the current achievements, the great and bright future can be predicted.

Finally, I want to mention serial comics. If my memory is correct, then it seems that only Xu Lunyin's "Before Sunrise" is a complete serial comic in this exhibition, which is about the experiences of a primary school teacher. Mr. Xu and Mr. Jin Jingye were the earliest initiators of the National Woodcut Joint Exhibition. Now Mr. Jin has brought these works to the eyes of the Shanghai people, but Mr. Xu quietly left this world a few weeks ago. I really mourn for him.

Although Chinese woodcut painting originated the earliest, it has always been despised and suppressed, and it has almost declined to the point where it is invisible. Now, to compare this little bit of achievement with countries such as Germany, France, England, and the Soviet Union, it is certainly very immature. Because we really don't have Frans Masereel, Meffert, Conatant Le Breton, Pamela'dA．Nalhan, N．I．Piskarev, and V．Konashevich. However, we already have efforts, and flowers blooming from these efforts. We expect them to be bright, beautiful, and lush.

This is a hope I have after seeing the National Woodcut Joint Exhibition.

A Certain Night (Part 1) 184

— Xi Cun

Just as darkness and light are two opposite contrasts, night and day are also completely different. In the dark night, you cannot see the clear sky and the flying white clouds as you can in the daytime; all that is presented before you is a dim sky and sparse stars; at night, you cannot see the road ahead as clearly as you can in the daytime, and the range of your vision is only a limited area of shadows. The streetlights make the night extra dull. The bustling scene of the daytime is completely transformed into calmness at night. Yes, the roads at night stretch out with a quiet solitude everywhere.

At that time, because of my work, I had to walk along a long, snake-like road every night. The time was always around midnight. The streets at that time were really quiet, with no one around, only the flickering shadows and heavy footsteps closely accompanying my loneliness. And sometimes, due to a sudden gust of wind, one or two fallen leaves would fly down from above, quietly gliding onto the road without a sound. Speaking of which, the roads in autumn are never short of fallen leaves.

Walking alone on a quiet road is very meaningful. At that time, the sense of hearing is the most acute. Even the smallest sounds in the distance, like the sound of sweeping the floor and the sound of shop signs fluttering, can be heard very clearly. Not to mention the sound of car horns and factory motors, which are even clearer.

One night, at the same time, I was walking on the road again as usual, preparing to return to my pigeon-nest-like room to rest for the night. When I was less than halfway there, I seemed to hear someone shouting nearby. At first, I couldn't make out the words, but later I heard them clearly.

"Selling children—who—wants to buy—children?"

The sound was drawn out for a long time, which clearly suggested to me that the person shouting must not have had enough energy, and from that weak sound, I could guess that there seemed to be some kind of embarrassing hidden pain in it.

I remembered something. In the past few days, haven't I been seeing some shocking news in the newspaper every day? Those news were all published on the front page of the newspaper with large headlines, water, water, that is to say, floods, from south to north, from east to west, almost the entire country was covered with floodwaters. And every time I saw those continuously published flood reports, it often aroused a sense of sadness and grief. At that time, I was sad for the victims on the one hand, and on the other hand, I naturally thought of the neglect of river conservancy projects. The newspaper also said that some victims had come to Shanghai. I heard that the local authorities were trying to disperse them far away in order to prevent accidents and create trouble. But where were they going, I thought at the time, wasn't there water everywhere?

Therefore, it made me think that perhaps the victims were crying out in pain! They had no home, and it was natural for them to spend the night on the road; they had no money, but they couldn't help but eat, so they could only sell their children to find a solution. This would not only allow them to eat a few more meals, but would it also reduce their burden? However, children are ultimately their flesh and blood, so they are still somewhat reluctant, which makes their throats not very comfortable when shouting; they certainly hope to find a buyer for their children, but they are also hoping that their children will not be sold!

"Selling children—who—wants to buy—children?"

The second shout came out again, and I happened to walk in front of them at this time. Outside the wall of a Western-style building, in a place where they could avoid the wind, three people were lying there. The light of the street lamps was able to reflect their three gray faces. The man and woman were middle-aged, probably husband and wife, and the child, with a snotty face, was about four or five years old, naturally their child. They were all wearing clothes that were even worse than rags, and it was difficult to resist the cold of the night, and they were all shivering. They huddled together for warmth. I wasn't wrong, they were indeed refugees. The man gave me an unexpected and pitiful look, glanced over me, and then opened his mouth:

"Sir, do a good deed, buy the child, okay?"

I stood there blankly, without speaking. I didn't know what to say. Were they really three people? They were almost three skeletons. Their appearance of having no way forward and sitting and waiting for death was somewhat like cows and pigs being led into a slaughterhouse. Their life and death were in the hands of others. The woman took advantage of my silence and added in a hoarse voice:

"Sir, there's no way, the water in the house, alas, the water flooded it. The house, the fields, all flooded. There's no way. Sir, please do a good deed and buy the child."

Remembering the Summer in Bōsō 185

— Xiangshan

Summer, the sea breeze brings the aroma of ripe fruit, mixed with the fresh scent of seaweed. What a vast and vibrant atmosphere!

Cotton-like clouds pile up in the melancholic sky. Gray seagulls glide along the coast, tracing arcs and net-like shapes in the sky. This leisurely soaring and dancing inspires and guides those weary of travel and burdened with sorrow.

The Tokyo Bay, nestled between the Bōsō Peninsula and the Miura Peninsula, stretches flatly beneath the sky, breeding countless seeds of imagination and contemplation. And the boundless Pacific Ocean, at the tip of the peninsula, seems to have witnessed millions of years of cosmic history without feeling a thing, relentlessly crashing wave after wave against the lighthouse standing tall in the azure sky.

Since moving to Hōjō on the Bōsō Peninsula, I have shifted my world-weary gaze to the vast sea and the green mountains winding along the peninsula. When the sea breeze passes through the green cypress forest along the coast, it lightly climbs over the lush rice paddies and rushes into the thick hills, emitting a loud and startling sound that pierces the heavens and the earth. At this moment, the sparrows perched on the ridge of the shrine on the hillside scatter in a flurry, like sesame seeds scattered across the sky. And the chirping noise, along with the tearing sound of the shrine's large flag ripped halfway by the wind, shatters the caretaker's sweet dreams under the eaves.

Ah, the sea is magnificent and indifferent! Relying on this boundless sea, I reflect on my own trivial daily life and truly feel small and ashamed.

In the morning, before the village path hears any footsteps, I open the window and wander in the small courtyard of eight square feet. The clear dew clings to the long sleeves of my kimono. This dew is as clear as tears, like what soaks the pillow and sleeves after waking from a dream of farewell.

When drawing clear, cold water from the well covered with morning glories to wash my face, I can't help but recite the haiku by Kaga no Chiyo:

"Morning glories twine

around the bucket. For you,

I borrow well water

from my neighbor."

From this haiku, one can feel a woman's gentle nature. Unable to bear plucking the morning glories twining around the bucket, she cannot draw water and has to borrow it from a neighbor. This love for living things is what I yearn for! But this is only a thing of the past!

When the white sun spreads golden light across the universe, I climb Castle Mountain in Nishihama and look down. The white sandy beach is quietly lapped by the seawater. The colorful swimsuits, worn by children, are like wildflowers of red, green, and yellow, scattered on the beach. And the straw hats placed on the rocks, like forgotten embers fading away, lazily lie dormant. Here and there, parasols, like poisonous mushrooms after rain, are scattered. At this time, twenty or thirty fishermen and fisherwomen are hauling in fishing nets in the distance. The water droplets falling from the nets reflect the sunlight, sparkling with five colors. A rhythmic chorus of folk songs rises. In the sea, a sailboat, full of sea breeze, carries a boatload of sunlight, crushing the golden waves and speeding away.

Looking at this seaside scenery, I am reminded of the short story "At the Bay" by the beautiful English writer Katherine Mansfield. Although this bay is not a Crescent Bay, doesn't her delicate writing fit the Tateyama Bay below?

Just as I was lost in thought, the call of a mountain bird suddenly rang out from the pine tree I was leaning against.

Ah! The sea is full of joy and happiness, making people forget all the hardships of life, sinking into a state of oblivion like a dream—when half-asleep on the armrest. When the village rooster crows its long midday announcement, the old people in the seaside village are struggling to keep their heavy eyelids open under the grape trellis.

At this time, only the bright sunlight and the sound of cicadas in the bushes, like oil being cut, fill the heavens and the earth. And from this noisy sound, I can feel the troubles of reality and at the same time realize a state of silence. Is the soul always tormented by this noisy reality? Or is it silently resisting? At this moment, a summer cloud covers the gingko tree, and a sorrowful expression and shadow appear on the delicate lily petals. Although the lily is planted in the shade of the large leaves of the Fatsia japonica, it is afraid of the threat of the approaching summer rain, feeling the same trembling and absent-mindedness!

I worry, I feel the terror of suffocation. A cool breeze blows from the sea, bringing the laughter and songs of young people on the beach, but I feel my heart is even more stirred up. When the wind chime hanging under the eaves rings with a clear sound, I look up at the sky. A seagull soars across the sky, leaving an image of freedom in my eyes. At this time, the distant mountains and nearby hills are lush, as if steamed and burst open. When I look around again at the quiet state of the small courtyard and my own peacefulness leaning on the armrest, I feel an indescribable taste.

'Lying down, leisurely watching the floating clouds, in the summer room.'

This haiku by Shida Noe describes the behavior of a poet gazing at the free and pure clouds in a comfortable room full of greenery. What a transcendent realm! Alas! Let my eyes close! I fall asleep in an ignorant dream, letting the murmuring sound of the Shiomi River flow by the traveler's pillow.

When I wake up, darkness sweeps over from the other side of the sea. The mountains are green and dim in the dusk, and a haze rises from the water's edge, making it difficult to distinguish. In the distance, the sound of the village's Bon dance drums fills my ears, and the seaside theater also plays music to attract customers. When I look up at the western corner of the house, a blood-red sunset hangs on top of the fire lookout tower.

Night has arrived, and the sea's moisture penetrates the bones. The landlord's child claps his small hands and points to the inky black sky, slowly singing a nursery rhyme:

One star seen,

Beside the clouds yo!

Two stars seen,

In…

………………

Large Belly Salt (Woodcut) 186

— Yefu

Honorable Old Woman (9) 187

— Written by Ema Shū, Translated by Ren Jun

In my house, everyone gathered around and comforted the old woman. Aside from saying that although this was undoubtedly a sad thing, it was actually a very honorable thing, there was no other way to comfort her. In particular, my mother also talked about the Yasukuni Shrine in Tokyo; she earnestly told her that the war dead were enshrined there, and that there were grand festivals twice a year, and that no matter how noble people were, they had to go there to worship.

While my mother was speaking, the old woman became calmer. And, just as if she were listening to a rare sermon, while constantly shedding tears, she deeply nodded to every word, listening as if she were very satisfied.

"From what you say," she said, sniffing, "it really makes me feel very unworthy. Now, I really understand what honor is all about. Thank you. It's really an honor, honor! I'm going to go back and tell my husband properly. Even so, but... that Yuzo..."

Speaking of Yuzo, she burst into tears again. My mother tried to persuade her with various words, and then asked the shopkeeper to accompany her and take her home.

According to later, more detailed reports, Yuzo died in the terrible attack on 203 Hill. He had always been admired for his bravery and boldness. That day, he also stood at the head of the assault team in the hail of bullets. When he fell, his body had already been hit by twenty-three bullets. Moreover, after people moved him into the tent, he survived for another ten hours.

He was immediately promoted to corporal, and because of his outstanding achievements, he also received the Golden Kite Medal, Sixth Class of Merit. A corporal with the Sixth Class of Merit was really an exceptional thing. There were very few precedents. And a consolation payment of three hundred taels was also issued.

The cooking old woman was very proud and unusually elated.

"How about that, Sixth Class of Merit, huh! He's a Corporal. Even the town elder can't match my son. Congratulations, congratulations, what could be more honorable and happier than this!"

Then she ran up to my mother and said:

"Look, madam! I can get three hundred dollars, I'm just completely dreaming. Think about it, three hundred taels, that's no small amount of money. We haven't seen such a large sum of money in our lives, thinking about it makes my head spin. Even so, but I've almost become a rich person!"

"It really is a good thing," my mother replied, "that's because you have an able son. Don't you see, the people in the town are all admiring you. They're all saying, 'This is not only your personal honor, but also the honor of everyone in the town.'"

The old woman cried with joy, her eyes full of tears.

"Thinking about it, my son is really pitiful; but I also feel that he really died well. Although the person is dead, the soul is still there; being worshiped by people in the Yasukuni Shrine in Tokyo, he won't have any dissatisfaction. As the old saying goes: 'Life is only for one lifetime, but reputation lasts for a thousand years.'"

"Of course. Even so, the government is really kind and very grateful."
